< Text>
I have been going to Ventura Bike Depot for several years, and have always had a great experience. Beginning with the purchase of a commuter bike in 2006 and several bike purchases last year. However, as much as getting a great deal on a sparky new bike is just awesome, the customer service is where this shop shines. I can get a cool new bike just about anywhere.....but....I can't walk into Amazon with my cousin looking for a cotter pin to piece together an old unicycle we found and were refurbishing, explain to the repair tech what we needed, then he rummages through a parts bin, come up with the part, and wouldn't charge us for it because it was just an old part he happened to have. We simply could not have finished that build without it. Every time I've been there, that is the level of customer service I've received.</Text>

< Text>
I shopped all of my local bike shops for a bit of advice (validation mostly)on bike fitment issues that I was having with my current road bike. I was commonly met with the standard, "it's gonna cost..." with prices ranging from $50.00 - $125
00. Which is fine. I get it. You're in business to be in business. No problem. But, Wait! What?. I have to wait a week? Really???

That wasn't the case when calling on, Ventura Bike Depot. I was listened to, as in "I hear you". Told that I could swing by anytime I'd like so that my issues could be further discussed at length. Once there, Alternative solutions were offered, discussed, and considerations reviewed, and not once was I made to feel that I was somehow imposing on their time. The end result was a discussion that lasted all of about ten minutes, validation and peace of mind over what I had already suspected to be the most viable solution. And the kicker, "No Charge". What?!?.

The bottom line for this establishment here is simply, " Client first and foremost" How could I not leave my Road Cycle there to be worked on. (Which I did)

If you're looking for excellent knowledgeable service and solid ethos in a company, then look no further. This is that place.</Text>

Bob Whiles<//name>
< review>
Fair pricing, good selection and good service - trustworthy.

I have done business with U Sav-Mor over the last 10 years.  I have found them to be both professional and knowledgeable.  As  a professional painter with experience in technical coatings as well as automotive finishes in restorations, detail is important to me and have found that I can get the information that I need to help me make a wise decision when selecting materials that I may not have experience with or a material for a special application.

I can understand why they ask for paint codes.  For those who complain - just because you don't understand doesn't mean that they are wrong.  Depending on when the car was built in any given year there can be more than one paint color that looks similar - You can't just say I need the light blue color for 2015 - there can be more than one shade that looks similar depending on when the car was built.  They can't be mixing paint based on what you think the color is.  If you are wrong they pay for it not you so they should ask if you have the paint code - automotive paint is expensive.

This store can be very busy and someone who is trying to help multiple people at one time may seem like they are rude when all they are is busy and you just take it the wrong way.  Personally I get it.  Sometimes my favorite person there doesn't have the time and I have to wait my turn,  call back or wait for them to call me back - BUT they always call back!   Maybe some people are the type that offend easily - I am not.

I can buy paint and materials from anyone that I want to.  I have accounts with other suppliers.  I choose to do business with Sav-Mor because they can be trusted.

Beware of negative reviews - I found that looking at a few of the negative reviewers complain a lot about everyone - I think you have to consider the source or read between the lines to see if they are just unhappy people in general with nothing to contribute</review>

< Review>
UPDATE 2
I tried to heal my dog's blockage up his nose on my own, but my dog had several seizures last night so I brought him to this vet on an emergency basis. Because my dog needed diagnostic tests that this emergency vet has on-site, and I was told several weeks ago that if I'd come in on an emergency basis he would be seen to have such tests, I came back here. The doctor I had last time Dr. Peck, told me that I could not have a diagnostic test through the emergency basis, that I would have to schedule a month out through the internal medicine department. After several conversations Dr. Peck transfered me to Internal Medicine Department who had agreed (Isabella) to schedule the needed tests on an emergency basis. I was then transferred to Dr. Peck who said no, that my dog who has had 3 seizures today is stable and not in need of emergency testing.  Am picking up my very sick dog now.

UPDATE
have my dog at the VCA emergency vet. They have informed me that they do have a liquid form of antibiotic that does not require a great amount of liquid, therefore a viable option. They also have offered which this vet did not, a shot, which is something I didn't even think of at the time, but should have been offered to me. I am flabbergasted at the lack of thought, concern and ability in the treatment of my dog at this facility. < text>
Our vet, Coastal Mobile Vet, recommended AVS to perform additional diagnostic testing, specifically an x ray and ultrasound after 2 previous blood panels didn't provide a cause to my cat's increasing weight loss.
I phoned AVS detailing my cat's symptoms, our vet's referral, and to ensure they had availability to perform the x -ray and ultrasound required. Per their instruction, we arrived at the clinic the following day at 5am and released our beloved cat to their care. 14 hours and over$1,500 later, I picked up my cat with no diagnosis, and a large cut to his ear while in AVS car.  AVS only suggested further testing, to include an endoscopy and colonoscopy, with their Internal Medicine Doctor, Isabel. It took some effort to reach her, but when I finally did, she said the soonest she could have a consultation would be two+ weeks out. At the rapid rate my cat was losing weight, I told her that he didn't have two weeks to wait and would likely die. Very coldly, she responded, "I am sorry, but I can't help you. Can I help you with anything else?"
With my cat's well-being my priority, I phoned AVS again and implored the on-call Doctor, Elizabeth Peck, for an appointment with Internal Medicine sooner. While she didn't have the authority over that dept., she urged us to return with my cat back to perform a GI Panel--which should have been done the first visit--to check his vitamin levels,  and other potential GI issues. Dr. Peck was very pleasant, compassionate, and empathized with our situation. However, her staff failed to inform me that my cat needed to be fasting for this exam which resulted in yet another visit to the hospital the following day. Dr. Peck prescribed a few medications to help my cat in the interim of the GI panel results--available within 48 hours.

Two days passed, no results. I called again 3 days later and was told they had only "partial results", but to phone again later.
On my third call, I spoke with the on-call doctor who explained she in fact had his results--revealing a strong indication for Inflammatory Bowel Disease [IBD]--and would email the full exam to me.
Hours pass, no email. I phone to request again the exam report and I'm told by the receptionist that she " will get this emailed to [you ]shortly".
3 hours pass, I phone again and speak to "Lisa," that makes a contradictory statement, "I am sorry but we haven't received the results yet". After numerous calls, waiting on hold, I am understandably frustrated which Lisa senses and is offended, she passes me on to another person.
A very unprofessional, ill mannered staff member abruptly told me he was going to "take care of the problem" and he "didn't have any time to discuss further with me" why I had to call 5 times to obtain test results. Before I could even ask his name, he said goodbye and hung up. I had to call back to ask his name so I could inform Management about his rude behavior. I learned that this man named Matt, was in fact the Manager!
AVS does not care about animals nor provide optimal care, and the majority of their staff lack decency and respect.
What AVS does excel in is invoicing and collecting payment quickly. I was charged an extra ultra sound fee on the same day because the staff did not instruct us to fast, and there was food in my cat's intestine. Another staff member said the extra charge was for "squeezing in the unscheduled" appointment--even though I had made an appointment the day before to schedule the ultrasound specifically. The GI panel,  cost another $525 and took two extra trips to AVS because again, no one informed me that my cat needed to be fasted. This test should have been done, admitted by their own On-Call Doctor, the very first visit based on his symptoms.
VCA (another animal hospital), saw us the very next day. Dr. Claudia (internal med) reviewed my cat's history, asked numerous questions, administered a shot of vitamin B12--before the GI panel results were available knowing his vitamin levels were likely low, and  reviewed a treatment plan for IBD. VCA is an incredible place to bring your pets!<//text>

RE: AVS & The Surgical Team

When told that treating any customer that poorly was uncalled for, let alone one who had spent over $10,000 at their establishment, and that I did not understand his hostility, Dr. Ayl decided that my pets and I were no longer welcome at the hospital and hung up the phone. And all this over an issue that I couldn't care less about, and didn't feel any need to discuss with him in the first place. Making me wonder why if his staff is so competent and infallible he felt the need to spend ten minutes berating me about how any misunderstandings were entirely my fault and that "I should have known better".  If his staff is so capable, why did he need to pull the phone from them and take it upon himself to lecture me on all the ways in which he was right and I was wrong.  I guess there is one thing that outweighs his greed, and that would be his arrogance.  I am saddened by this turn of events with the hospital, and can no longer trust my animals around someone so negative and disrespectful. Not that I have a choice, as rather than be civil to a client, one doctor there has now decided to make my pets suffer by kicking them to the curb and making me find another place much further away to take over their care. Leaving them without necessary medication in the meantime.  Shameful behavior for a doctor.  From what I read of reviews online though, this is a common problem, among others. Medication and machines that these doctors possess can perhaps help your animal, but if you can go anywhere else for those, I would. No help from anyone is worth the abusive an unreasonable attitude of this office.  Hopefully this review will encourage them to reign in the attitude a bit and start treating their customers with some modicum of respect.

And while I'm writingâ€¦. another problem here is that the office deals exclusively in old world solutions to cancer and chronic conditions. The sell radiation and chemo drugs.  We all know that is the past and not the future, and it would be nice to see medical professionals that are at least somewhat aware of other options and have some information to offer.  Real alternatives would be great, like pet formulated CBD treatments, which have been shown to be extremely effective.  From my experience though nobody at this office wants to discuss other options, they're just too eager to get you to sign off up for the $5,000-20,000 radiation therapies they offer.  Business over medicine, which is a dead wrong approach to healthcare.< /Review>< pictures>

< text>
Like all ER's, AVS is VERY expensive, and I was very fortunate to have CareCredit when I recently had need of their services for one of my animals who developed a life-threatening infection.

The level of compassion, caring, and competence of AVS was absolutely marvelous. The facility is immaculate, the lobby is nicely decorated and inviting. The staff were all very efficient and kind, and I never felt that my animal was just a number to them. There was no patronizing attitude and NO anti-breeder or anti-purebred vibe at ALL. We felt valued on all levels in a way that was nothing like my experience several years ago with the other local ER, which was so unpleasant that I don't even want to describe it.

AVS is a wonderful addition to Santa Barbara...my only wish is that it existed up in Lompoc, where we live. There is nothing anywhere near here for a veterinary ER: everything is an hour away in SB or an hour the other way in Arroyo Grande, leaving this area completely without. I spent several days driving back and forth with my sick pet to AVS, and again...I sure wish we had them up here!

I hope AVS succeeds, and continues to provide its excellent service and the CHOICE of ERs in the SB area. Choice is good. AVS is excellent. Thank you for the great care, kindness, and genuine concern for the welfare of my animal!<//text>

<Time>1620920248457<//Time><name>Allan Chu</name><Text>We had a fantastic time dining at Sommâ€™s Kitchen run by the multitalented Ian. Conceptually the experience is a surprise tasting menu supercharged with trophy wines and liquors. This all takes place at a 12 seat curved bar where you can see Ian assemble each menu item. Ian slow prepares the items in advance using slow cooking, curing, sous vide, etc. and then finishes the dishes in front of you. The food is great but then he uses his sommelier background to pair wines and in our case bourbons with each course. And not just any wines or bourbons, Ian is looking to take the mystique out of the trophy or cult brands (like Bryant Family, Saxum, Sine Qua Non, Stagg) and happily pours these to get diner reactions. The result by the end of the night will leave you in a state of rapture and eager to plan your next visit.< /Text>< Rating>

Iâ€™m still on the fence on this one.  On one hand I had a great experience wine tasting.   Food was tasty but left me quite hungry.  Had to go eat a real meal afterwards.

Let me explain.

About a dozen of you sit around a long circular bar type counter.  Owner/chef assembles small dishes that he pairs with wine.   Food is not cooked in front of you and is fairly easy to pull off.  Chef claims to have worked at a Michelin restaurant but these are not fancy dishes.

We had appetizers like sliced meats and cheese.  Also a warm soup.   Then came a chunk of salmon and a bit of steak.   Each dish was quite good but did not quite make a meal.  And Iâ€™m a small guy who typically does not eat much.

Each dish, however, was paired with a wine.  Wine education and pairing is the real strength here.    We had two kinds of bubblies, whites and reds.   They all quite good and paired really well.   When your glass was empty he would pour some more.   So that part was quite nice.

The seating is a bit peculiar.  Some people get the good seats and get to see what he is doing and others sit on the sides and donâ€™t get much of his attention.  The people who came the latest (the ones we all had to wait for) got the best seats so not sure how that works.

Part of the way through another group enters and they sit in a back room.   Now they get part of the chefâ€™s attention too.

Overall it was a fun experience. There was plenty of good wine to drink, but donâ€™t expect a filling meal.  Would I go back?   Yah, likely, but Iâ€™d eat first.</review>

<name>Tamara Scholtz<//name>< resp>

0x80ecc567f7e71789:0x931fabd7ab7b7890</GmapID>
< Rate>

< pictures>
None<//pictures>
< text>
I love walking into a new situation and not being exactly sure what I'm about to experience.  I love even more walking out thinking I can't WAIT to tell others that they need to experience this, too!

I think if people consider going to Somm's kitchen buying a ticket to an experience instead of paying a bill for dinner they'll get far more out of the ride.

On March 9, my husband and I were visiting Somm's kitchen from Austin, Texas.  We had been in Paso for the first time last year before this restaurant opened, so we were excited to try something new on the square.  We made a reservation about a month before.  When we walked in, Ian told us our spot was at the end of his semi circular bar which had enough room for about 14 people.

Ian greeted us and asked, "Are you hungry?"  We stated we were, and he handed us a glass of a most interesting Austrian sparkling wine.  We had no menu in front of us, wine or otherwise.  There was nothing to suggest what we might be eating, what we might be drinking, how many courses there may be, or even how much things might cost.

I'm sure we could have asked Ian, but we decided we were in for the ride!  For the next two hours we were in his hands as he had us try a local cheese, a foie gras that rivaled that of Michelin starred restaurants, a prime filet, lamb, and on and on...

It seemed some people came and went and didn't stay for the whole ride.  I'm not sure if all the kinks are ironed out there, but it didn't hinder our experience at all.

Each course was served with about a half of a glass of wine...unless of course you drank your wine, then more showed up.  None of the wines were particularly expensive, but all were particularly wonderful and the best paired I've ever had with any food ANYWHERE (and not to get all foodie/wine snobby... but we've been to Picasso, Cyrus, Robuchon... the pairing at Somm's Kitchen was simply AMAZING!)

The whole time we felt as though we were Ian's guests.  He chatted to us about the wines and the food and how he had prepared each thing.  At one point, he stopped and gave us a lesson in wine tasting.  It was taught in such a way that novice and experienced wine aficionados a like could enjoy. Ian is an experienced sommelier who teachers wine classes internationally, so getting a chance to experience this was quite a thrill!

In the French style, Ian prepared a salad between the final course and the desserts.  The salad was so creative.  He peeled the quail eggs and prepared it in front of us.  He carefully cut and placed herbs from right to left and as you ate, the herbs and the flavors increased in intensity with each bite.

We finished with desserts and feeling like we had made friends with our fellow diners and our host.

Our final bill was $250 for the two of us.  Both my husband and I felt this was truly a bargain.  We have paid more for less in the past.

Now, for the "to be completely honest" parts.  I would have liked a menu at least when we left if not to follow at the time.  Ian did say that I could email him and he would send a menu with all the information.  I intend to do that, but it would have been nice to look over it that evening, or even as I was writing this review.

Also, I'm not sure exactly how he decided who got what food.  There was a woman sitting next to me who I ran into twice again in the week while we were there.  Each time I saw her someplace else, she was telling other people that she was upset that she asked for potatoes and didn't get them even though some people did.  She did not like her experience at all and thought Ian was rude.  I thought he was funny and dry.  I liked his sense of humor, but I could see where others might find him off putting.  He's a New Yorker, not a Californian... and he still has some of the edge.

I also heard some complain about the price.   I think ANYWHERE you go 11 courses and 11 half glasses of wine for $125 a person is an amazing bargain... but I understand if you're thinking your'e only going to spend $50 on dinner.. this would be a little rough.<//text>
